        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  With significant recent advancements in thermal sciences-such as the development of new theor. and exptl. techniques, and the discovery of new transport mechanisms-it is helpful to revisit the fundamentals of vibrational heat conduction to formulate an updated and informed phys. understanding.  The increasing maturity of simulation and modeling methods sparks the desire to leverage these techniques to rapidly improve and develop technol. through digital engineering and multi-scale, electro-thermal models.  With that vision in mind, this review attempts to build a holistic understanding of thermal transport by focusing on the often unaddressed relationships between subfields, which can be crit. for multi-scale modeling approaches.  For example, we outline the relationship between mode-specific (computational) and spectral (anal.) models.  We relate thermal boundary resistance models based on perturbation approaches and classic transmissivity based models.  We discuss the relationship between lattice dynamics and mol. dynamics approaches along with two-channel transport frameworks that have emerged recently and that connect crystal-like and amorphous-like heat conduction.  Throughout, we discuss best practices for modeling exptl. data and outline how these models can guide material-level and system-level design.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Many low-thermal-cond. (κL) crystals show intriguing temp. (T) dependence of κL: κL .varies. T-1 (crystal-like) at intermediate temps. whereas weak T-dependence (glass-like) at high temps.  It has been in debate whether thermal transport can still be described by phonons at the Ioffe-Regel limit.  In this work, we propose that most phonons are still well defined for thermal transport, whereas they carry heat via dual channels: normal phonons described by the Boltzmann transport equation theory, and diffuson-like phonons described by the diffusion theory.  Three physics-based criteria are incorporated into first-principles calcns. to judge mode-by-mode between the two phonon channels.  Case studies on La2Zr2O7 and Tl3VSe4 show that normal phonons dominate low temps. while diffuson-like phonons dominate high temps.  Our present dual-phonon theory enlightens the physics of hierarchical phonon transport as approaching the Ioffe-Regel limit and provides a numerical method that should be practically applicable to many materials with vibrational hierarchy.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ioffe, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Crystals and glasses exhibit fundamentally different heat conduction mechanisms: the periodicity of crystals allows for the excitation of propagating vibrational waves that carry heat, as first discussed by Peierls, while in glasses the lack of periodicity breaks Peierls's picture and heat is mainly carried by the coupling of vibrational modes, often described by a harmonic theory introduced by Allen and Feldman.  Anharmonicity or disorder are thus the limiting factors for thermal cond. in crystals or glasses.  Hitherto, no transport equation has been able to account for both.  Here, we derive such an equation, resulting in a thermal cond. that reduces to the Peierls and Allen-Feldman limits, resp., in anharmonic crystals or harmonic glasses, while also covering the intermediate regimes where both effects are relevant.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmueller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.77.3865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Perdew, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">ShengBTE is a software package for computing the lattice thermal cond. of cryst. bulk materials and nanowires with diffusive boundary conditions.  It is based on a full iterative soln. to the Boltzmann transport equation.  Its main inputs are sets of second- and third-order interat. force consts., which can be calcd. using third-party ab-initio packages.  Dirac delta distributions arising from conservation of energy are approximated by Gaussian functions.  A locally adaptive algorithm is used to det. each process-specific broadening parameter, which renders the method fully parameter free.  The code is free software, written in Fortran and parallelized using MPI.  A complementary Python script to help compute third-order interat. force consts. from a min. no. of ab-initio calcns., using a real-space finite-difference approach, is also publicly available for download.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Crystal structure of NaVO3 was refined at room temp. (ferroelec. phase) and 425° (paraelec. phase) using x-ray diffraction data.  The structural change during the ferroelec. phase transition is only a slight modification of the paraelec. phase.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bonding Hierarchy Gives Rise to High Thermoelectric Performance in Layered Zintl Compound BaAu2P4</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pal, Koushik; He, Jiangang; Wolverton, C.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7760-7768</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The search for new thermoelec. materials has gained rapid progress in recent years as thermoelec. technol. offers the potential for environmentally friendly and sustainable energy conversion methods from waste heat to electricity.  The authors use 1st-principles calcns. based on d. functional theory to predict high thermoelec. performance in BaAu2P4, a layered Zintl compd. with a small band gap.  BaAu2P4 exhibits crystallog. heterogeneity in which rigid [Au2P4]2- units are sepd. by layers of Ba2+ cations, which are bonded relatively weakly to the lattice through electrostatic interactions.  The phosphorus atoms are covalently bonded to each other and form infinite chains within the crystal.  While the phosphorus chains facilitate large elec. cond., the presence of multiple bands near the Fermi level gives rise to an enhanced Seebeck coeff.  However, the loosely bound Ba along with Au strongly scatter the heat carrying acoustic phonons, significantly reducing the lattice thermal conduction along the stacking direction.  As a consequence of this bonding hierarchy (i.e., coexisting rigid and fluctuating sublattices), BaAu2P4 exhibits a large power factor and low lattice thermal cond., which results in a high thermoelec. figure of merit (zT).  Thus, the authors' findings should encourage the exploration of new thermoelec. materials in the family of layered compds. with small band gaps and crystallog. heterogeneity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104822"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper thiocyanate (CuSCN) has recently received considerable attention because of its high hole mobility and applications in solar cells [Science 358(2017)768].  In this work, by performing state-of-the-art theor. calcns., for the first time we find that the thermal conductivities of both α- and β-CuSCN are ultralow with the values of 1.2 and 2.4 W/mK at room temp., resp.  Based on detailed analyses of the phonon dispersion, Gruneisen parameters, three phonon scattering rates and at. displacement parameters, we further demonstrate that the underlying reasons for the ultralow thermal conductivities are due to the avoided crossing between the longitudinal acoustic (LA) phonons and the low-lying optical branches as well as the weak bonding and strong anharmonicity.  The low lattice thermal conductivities lead to high ZT values of 1.7 and 2.1 at 800 K for α- and β-CuSCN, resp.  In addn., both materials exhibit large neg. thermal expansion (NTE) coeffs. originated from the transverse vibrations in Cu-N-C-S chains.  These features endow CuSCN with the potential for thermal barrier coating and thermal devices going beyond the reported photovoltaic applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201904862"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cagnoni, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cojocaru-Mirédin, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wuttig, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chalcogenide Thermoelectrics Empowered by an Unconventional Bonding Mechanism</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chalcogenide Thermoelectrics Empowered by an Unconventional Bonding Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Yuan; Cagnoni, Matteo; Cojocaru-Miredin, Oana; Wuttig, Matthias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Thermoelec. materials have attracted significant research interest in recent decades due to their promising application potential in interconverting heat and electricity.  Unfortunately, the strong coupling between the material parameters that det. thermoelec. efficiency, i.e., the Seebeck coeff., elec. cond., and thermal cond., complicates the optimization of thermoelec. energy converters.  Main-group chalcogenides provide a rich playground to alleviate the interdependence of these parameters.  Interestingly, only a subgroup of octahedrally coordinated chalcogenides possesses good thermoelec. properties.  This subgroup is also characterized by other outstanding characteristics suggestive of an exceptional bonding mechanism, which has been coined metavalent bonding.  This conclusion is further supported by a map that separates different bonding mechanisms.  In this map, all octahedrally coordinated chalcogenides with good performance as thermoelecs. are located in a well-defined region, implying that the map can be utilized to identify novel thermoelecs.  To unravel the correlation between chem. bonding mechanism and good thermoelec. properties, the consequences of this unusual bonding mechanism on the band structure are analyzed.  It is shown that features such as band degeneracy and band anisotropy are typical for this bonding mechanism, as is the low lattice thermal cond.  This fundamental understanding, in turn, guides the rational materials design for improved thermoelec. performance by tailoring the chem. bonding mechanism.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2021.162862"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pei, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A comprehensive experimental and first-principles study on magnesium-vanadium oxides</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Calcium pyrovanadate (Ca2V2O7) has been reported as an advanced functional material for optoelectronics and energy storage owing to its layered crystal structure and intense O2-V5+ charge transfer bands.  Therefore, the studies on the physicochem. properties of Ca2V2O7 to further improve its service performance are indispensable.  Herein, we systemically investigate the structural, lattice dynamic, and thermodn. properties of Ca2V2O7 utilizing exptl. measurements and first-principles calcns.  The measured heat capacity is found to obviously break through the Dulong-Petit limit, indicating that strong anharmonicity is present in Ca2V2O7.  Furthermore, we reveal the hierarchical thermal transport behavior of Ca2V2O7 in the dual-phonon theory framework and predict the ultralow lattice thermal cond. (κ) with values of 2.15, 2.11, and 1.91 W/mK along the a, b, and c axes at 300 K.  The results indicate that a significant contribution from diffusive thermal transport to the κ is obsd., leading to a temp.-dependent κ much flatter than that of the general law of κ ∼ T-1 in most other materials.  This study not only promotes the diverse applications of Ca2V2O7 such as thermal insulating materials and batteries but also provides novel insights into the fundamental thermal physics of calcium-intercalated layered vanadium-based oxides.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">King, E.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Four-phonon scattering significantly reduces intrinsic thermal conductivity of solids</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Tianli; Lindsay, Lucas; Ruan, Xiulin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">96</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For decades, the three-phonon scattering process has been considered to govern thermal transport in solids, while the role of higher-order four-phonon scattering has been persistently unclear and so ignored.However, recent quant. calcns. of three-phonon scattering have often shown a significant overestimation of thermal cond. as compared to exptl. values.  In this Rapid Communication we show that four-phonon scattering is generally important in solids and can remedy such discrepancies.  For silicon and diamond, the predicted thermal cond. is reduced by 30% at 1000 K after including four-phonon scattering, bringing predictions in excellent agreement with measurements.  For the projected ultrahigh-thermal cond. material, zinc-blende BAs, a competitor of diamond as a heat sink material, four-phonon scattering is found to be strikingly strong as three-phonon processes have an extremely limited phase space for scattering.  The four-phonon scattering reduces the predicted thermal cond. from 2200 to 1400 W/m K at room temp.  The redn. at 1000 K is 60%.  We also find that optical phonon scattering rates are largely affected, being important in applications such as phonon bottlenecks in equilibrating electronic excitations.  Recognizing that four-phonon scattering is expensive to calc., in the end we provide some guidelines on how to quickly assess the significance of four-phonon scattering, based on energy surface anharmonicity and the scattering phase space.  Our work clears the decades-long fundamental question of the significance of higher-order scattering, and points out ways to improve thermoelecs., thermal barrier coatings, nuclear materials, and radiative heat transfer.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.100.245203"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruan, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stronger role of four-phonon scattering than three-phonon scattering in thermal conductivity of III-V semiconductors at room temperature</span>. <i>Phys.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recent studies reveal that four-phonon scattering can be important in detg. thermal conductivities of solids.  However, these studies have been focused on materials where the thermal cond. κ is dominated by acoustic phonons, and the role of four-phonon scattering, although significant, is still smaller than that of three-phonon scattering at room temp.  In this work, taking AlSb as an example for which optical phonons contribute significantly to the thermal cond. under the three-phonon picture, we demonstrate that four-phonon scattering can be more important than three-phonon scattering as it diminishes optical phonon thermal transport and therefore significantly reduces the thermal conductivities of materials.  Also, our calcns. show that four-phonon scattering can diminish the isotope effect on κ.  Specifically, including four-phonon scattering reduces the room-temp. κ of isotopically pure BAs from 3322 W/mK to 1721 W/mK, a 48% redn.  Four-phonon scattering reduces the room-temp. κ of the isotopically pure and naturally occurring AlSb by 70% and 50%, resp., indicating that four-phonon scattering is more important than three-phonon scattering.  The redns. for isotopically pure and naturally occurring cubic GaN are about 34% and 27%, resp.  For isotopically pure wurtzite GaN, the redn. is about 13% at room temp. and 25% at 400 K.  These results provided important guidance for experimentalists for achieving high thermal conductivities in III-V compds. for applications in the semiconductor industry.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref50" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.126.115901"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kundu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carrete, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Madsen, G.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Abnormal in-plane thermal conductivity anisotropy in bilayer α-phase tellurene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Yanhua; Yang, Xiaolong; Han, Zherui; Wu, Wenzhuo; Luo, Xiaobing; Ruan, Xiulin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Heat and Mass Transfer</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">192</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">122908</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IJHMAK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0017-9310</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In layered materials, it is well known that the cross-plane or cross-chain (CC) thermal cond. is lower than that of the in-plane or along-chain direction due to weaker bonding in the cross-plane or CC directions.  In this work, surprisingly, we predict using first-principles that the CC thermal cond. κ.perp. is higher than the along-chain thermal cond. κ‖ with a κ.perp./κ‖ ratio of 1.174 in bilayer α-phase tellurene (2L-αTe), an emerging 2D material that has recently drawn extensive interest due to its intriguing electronic, thermoelectronic, and piezoelectronic properties.  Also, the room-temp. κ.perp. and κ‖ of 2L-αTe are 5.69 W/mK and 4.85 W/mK, which are 251% and 31% enhanced from that of bulk Te, resp.  A detailed anal. of lattice structure, phonon spectra, and electron properties of 2L-αTe and bulk Te is provided.  We find that the larger lattice shrink in CC direction and the change in band angle lead to stiffened phonons and weaker anharmonicity, which in turn yield higher phonon group velocity and longer phonon lifetime in CC direction for 2L-αTe, resulting in the enhanced thermal cond. and the anomolus thermal anisotropy.  Crystal orbital Hamiltan population (COHP) and electron localization function (ELF) anal. demonstrate the enhancement of the strength of "covalent-like quasi-bonding" (CLQB) in CC direction of 2L-αTe, which is accompanied by the lattice shrink in CC direction and the change of band angle.  Our study identifies a case of unexpected anisotropic thermal transport in 2D materials, and sheds light on the improvement of thermal cond. isotropy in 2D materials for the thermal management of electronic devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref54" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms4525"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Esfarjani, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Resonant bonding leads to low lattice thermal conductivity</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3525</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms4525</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D3525%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DS.%2BLee%26author%3DK.%2BEsfarjani%26author%3DT.%2BLuo%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DZ.%2BTian%26author%3DG.%2BChen%26title%3DResonant%2Bbonding%2Bleads%2Bto%2Blow%2Blattice%2Bthermal%2Bconductivity%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms4525&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.jpclett.2c03061&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms4525&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Resonant bonding leads to low lattice thermal conductivity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee Sangyeop; Zhou Jiawei; Tian Zhiting; Chen Gang; Esfarjani Keivan; Luo Tengfei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3525</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Understanding the lattice dynamics and low thermal conductivities of IV-VI, V2-VI3 and V materials is critical to the development of better thermoelectric and phase-change materials.  Here we provide a link between chemical bonding and low thermal conductivity.  Our first-principles calculations reveal that long-ranged interaction along the 〈100〉 direction of the rocksalt structure exist in lead chalcogenides, SnTe, Bi2Te3, Bi and Sb due to the resonant bonding that is common to all of them.  This long-ranged interaction in lead chalcogenides and SnTe cause optical phonon softening, strong anharmonic scattering and large phase space for three-phonon scattering processes, which explain why rocksalt IV-VI compounds have much lower thermal conductivities than zincblende III-V compounds.  The new insights on the relationship between resonant bonding and low thermal conductivity will help in the development of better thermoelectric and phase change materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref55" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.0c01710"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sato, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tobita, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kimura, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mori, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unusual Lattice Dynamics and Anisotropic Thermal Conductivity in In<sub>2</sub>Te<sub>5</sub> Due to a Layered Structure and Planar-Coordinated Te-Chains</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">5335</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5342</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemmater.0c01710</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D32%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D5335-5342%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26issue%3D12%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DN.%2BSato%26author%3DK.%2BTobita%26author%3DK.%2BKimura%26author%3DT.%2BMori%26title%3DUnusual%2BLattice%2BDynamics%2Band%2BAnisotropic%2BThermal%2BConductivity%2Bin%2BIn2Te5%2BDue%2Bto%2Ba%2BLayered%2BStructure%2Band%2BPlanar-Coordinated%2BTe-Chains%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemmater.0c01710&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.jpclett.2c03061&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.0c01710&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unusual Lattice Dynamics and Anisotropic Thermal Conductivity in In2Te5 Due to a Layered Structure and Planar-Coordinated Te-Chains</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenhao; Sato, Naoki; Tobita, Kazuki; Kimura, Kaoru; Mori, Takao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5335-5342</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Searching for novel materials with intrinsically low thermal cond. and uncovering their origin is an essential way to realize high performance in various energy-related applications, including thermoelecs.  Understanding the role of different structural features in materials can assist us in designing thermal transport properties.  Herein, we report thermal transport behavior of In2Te5, which is closely related to its layered zigzag structure and bonding in planar-coordinated Te-chains.  The exptl. thermal cond. shows significant anisotropy for the measured two directions and an extremely low value in the interlayer direction of about 0.3 W m-1 K-1 at 673 K.  The theor. calcns. of lattice thermal cond. based on d. functional theory support this behavior, and furthermore, they even reveal unprecedented anisotropy in the in-layer direction.  We demonstrate that these thermal transport behaviors can be attributed to resonant bonding and lattice dynamics obsd. at the Te atoms in the planar-coordinated environment.  Particularly strikingly, we discover a counterintuitive large pos. and neg. split of the Born effective charge (+8.7 and -5.1) at the adjacent Te atoms bonded covalently within the same plane.  They induce a significant dipole interaction in the x-direction.  Optical phonons are significantly softened in the specific direction by these characteristics in the Te-plane, which leads to large anisotropy in thermal transport.  Our findings should encourage further excavation of novel features in lattice dynamics out of unexplored materials with complex structures.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.101.035901"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morelli, D. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jovovic, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Heremans, J. P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Intrinsically Minimal Thermal Conductivity in Cubic I-V- VI2 Semiconductors</span>. <i>Phys. Rev. Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2008</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>101</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">035901</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1103/PhysRevLett.101.035901</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D101%26publication_year%3D2008%26pages%3D035901%26journal%3DPhys.%2BRev.%2BLett.%26issue%3D3%26author%3DD.%2BT.%2BMorelli%26author%3DV.%2BJovovic%26author%3DJ.%2BP.%2BHeremans%26title%3DIntrinsically%2BMinimal%2BThermal%2BConductivity%2Bin%2BCubic%2BI-V-%2BVI2%2BSemiconductors%26doi%3D10.1103%252FPhysRevLett.101.035901&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.jpclett.2c03061&amp;doiOfLink=10.1103%2FPhysRevLett.101.035901&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intrinsically minimal thermal conductivity in cubic I-V-VI2 semiconductors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Morelli, D. T.; Jovovic, V.; Heremans, J. P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">101</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">035901/1-035901/4</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0031-9007</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report measurements of the thermal cond. of high-quality crystals of the cubic I-V-VI2 semiconductors AgSbTe2 and AgBiSe2.  The thermal cond. is temp. independent from 80 to 300 K at a value of approx. 0.70 W/mK.  Heat conduction is dominated by the lattice term, which we show is limited by umklapp and normal phonon-phonon scattering processes to a value that corresponds to the min. possible, where the phonon mean free path equals the interat. distance.  Min. thermal cond. in cubic I-V-VI2 semiconductors is due to an extreme anharmonicity of the lattice vibrational spectrum that gives rise to a high Gruneisen parameter and strong phonon-phonon interactions.  Members of this family of compds. are therefore most promising for thermoelec. applications, particularly as p-type materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187dcd8d35075b-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47'],'ref48':['cit48'],'ref49':['cit49'],'ref50':['cit50'],'ref51':['cit51'],'ref52':['cit52'],'ref53':['cit53'],'ref54':['cit54'],'ref55':['cit55'],'ref56':['cit56']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy storage technologies are crit. in addressing the global challenge of clean sustainable energy.  Major advances in rechargeable batteries for portable electronics, elec. vehicles and large-scale grid storage will depend on the discovery and exploitation of new high performance materials, which requires a greater fundamental understanding of their properties on the at. and nanoscopic scales.  This review describes some of the exciting progress being made in this area through use of computer simulation techniques, focusing primarily on pos. electrode (cathode) materials for lithium-ion batteries, but also including a timely overview of the growing area of new cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  In general, two main types of technique have been employed, namely electronic structure methods based on d. functional theory, and atomistic potentials-based methods.  A major theme of much computational work has been the significant synergy with exptl. studies.  The scope of contemporary work is highlighted by studies of a broad range of topical materials encompassing layered, spinel and polyanionic framework compds. such as LiCoO2, LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4 resp.  Fundamental features important to cathode performance are examd., including voltage trends, ion diffusion paths and dimensionalities, intrinsic defect chem., and surface properties of nanostructures.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.0c02181"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abraham, K.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.0c02244"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goonetilleke, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sharma, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sit, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) are a potential low-cost alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale energy storage, but many high-capacity NIB cathode materials undergo irreversible structural changes during charge and discharge, leading to fast capacity fading.  Herein, monoclinic NaVO3 exhibits good cycle performance with high capacity as a cathode material for NIBs.  In situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction studies show that the material structure is virtually invariant during Na+ (de-)intercalation, with the a and b lattice parameters changing only by 0.13 and 0.19%, resp.  The material undergoes an oxygen redox reaction during initial charge while delivering a remarkable specific capacity of 245 mAh g-1 (1.2-4.7 V) with contributions from cationic (V4+/V5+) and anionic (O2-/O-) redox couples during discharge.  The stable VO4 tetrahedral framework also enables the material to give superior rate and cycle capabilities, with a capacity of 164 mAh g-1 (67% utilization) at a current of 1000 mA g-1 (about 5C) and a capacity retention of 90% after 50 cycles.  D. functional theory calcns. further verify the stability of the material and the charge-discharge mechanism.  This work can broaden the horizon for designing high-energy cathode materials with enhanced structural stability for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2021.230535"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wong, C.-P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemically incorporated Cu nanoparticles in NaVO<sub>3</sub> with enhanced sodium-ion battery performance</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are believed to be the promising low-cost candidates as compared to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  Particularly, layered metal oxides show great potential as electrode materials with high capacity for SIB.  However, the layered metal oxides undergo irreversible structural changes and suffer from low cond. during charge and discharge, leading to sluggish electrochem. processes and fast capacity fading.  To overcome these weaknesses, we electrochem. in-situ incorporate copper nanoparticles in NaVO3 host material during battery cycling processes, giving rise to fast electron transfer in the material matrix.  The resultant copper-incorporated NaVO3 is demonstrated to have significantly increased performance for SIBs, which exhibits excellent reversible capacity, high coulombic efficiency, large capacity retention and outstanding rate capability.  From ex-situ microscopy and spectroscopy characterizations, we show the evidence of the electrochem. formed Cu nanoparticles. Recent researches on sodium-rich compds. such as Na2RuO3 and Na2IrO3 suggest that anionic reaction with oxygen can be an addnl. source of electrons during electrochem. reactions.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Whether attempting to eliminate parasitic Li metal plating on graphite (and other Li-ion anodes) or enabling stable, uniform Li metal formation in 'anode-free' Li battery configurations, the detection and characterization (morphol., microstructure, chem.) of Li that cannot be reversibly cycled is essential to understand the behavior and degrdn. of rechargeable batteries.  In this review, various approaches used to detect and characterize the formation of Li in batteries are discussed.  Each technique has its unique set of advantages and limitations, and works towards solving only part of the full puzzle of battery degrdn.  Going forward, multimodal characterization holds the most promise towards addressing two pressing concerns in the implementation of the next generation of batteries in the transportation sector (viz. reducing recharging times and increasing the available capacity per recharge without sacrificing cycle life).         </div><div class="casAbstract">The physics of heat conduction puts practical limits on many technol. fields such as energy prodn., storage, and conversion.  It is now widely appreciated that the phonon-gas model does not describe the full vibrational spectrum in amorphous materials, since this picture likely breaks down at higher frequencies.  A two-channel heat conduction model, which uses harmonic vibrational states and lattice dynamics as a basis, has recently been shown to capture both crystal-like (phonon-gas channel) and amorphous-like (diffuson channel) heat conduction.  While materials design principles for the phonon-gas channel are well established, similar understanding and control of the diffuson channel is lacking.  In this work, in order to uncover design principles for the diffuson channel, we study structurally-complex cryst. Yb14 (Mn,Mg)Sb11, a champion thermoelec. material above 800 K, exptl. using inelastic neutron scattering and computationally using the two-channel lattice dynamical approach.  Our results show that the diffuson channel indeed dominates in Yb14MnSb11 above 300 K.  More importantly, we demonstrate a method for the rational design of amorphous-like heat conduction by considering the energetic proximity phonon modes and modifying them through chem. means.  We show that increasing (decreasing) the mass on the Sb-site decreases (increases) the energy of these modes such that there is greater (smaller) overlap with Yb-dominated modes resulting in a higher (lower) thermal cond.  This design strategy is exactly opposite of what is expected when the phonon-gas channel and/or common anal. models for the diffuson channel are considered, since in both cases an increase in at. mass commonly leads to a decrease in thermal cond.  This work demonstrates how two-channel lattice dynamics can not only quant. predict the relative importance of the phonon-gas and diffuson channels, but also lead to rational design strategies in materials where the diffuson channel is important.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1063/5.0055593"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hanus, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gurunathan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lindsay, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Agne, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Crystals and glasses exhibit fundamentally different heat conduction mechanisms: the periodicity of crystals allows for the excitation of propagating vibrational waves that carry heat, as first discussed by Peierls, while in glasses the lack of periodicity breaks Peierls's picture and heat is mainly carried by the coupling of vibrational modes, often described by a harmonic theory introduced by Allen and Feldman.  Anharmonicity or disorder are thus the limiting factors for thermal cond. in crystals or glasses.  Hitherto, no transport equation has been able to account for both. This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme. It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size. They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).         </div><div class="casAbstract">ShengBTE is a software package for computing the lattice thermal cond. of cryst. bulk materials and nanowires with diffusive boundary conditions.  It is based on a full iterative soln. to the Boltzmann transport equation.  Its main inputs are sets of second- and third-order interat. force consts., which can be calcd. using third-party ab-initio packages.  Dirac delta distributions arising from conservation of energy are approximated by Gaussian functions.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The search for new thermoelec. materials has gained rapid progress in recent years as thermoelec. technol. offers the potential for environmentally friendly and sustainable energy conversion methods from waste heat to electricity.  The authors use 1st-principles calcns. based on d. functional theory to predict high thermoelec. performance in BaAu2P4, a layered Zintl compd. with a small band gap.  BaAu2P4 exhibits crystallog. heterogeneity in which rigid [Au2P4]2- units are sepd. by layers of Ba2+ cations, which are bonded relatively weakly to the lattice through electrostatic interactions.  The phosphorus atoms are covalently bonded to each other and form infinite chains within the crystal.  While the phosphorus chains facilitate large elec. cond., the presence of multiple bands near the Fermi level gives rise to an enhanced Seebeck coeff.  However, the loosely bound Ba along with Au strongly scatter the heat carrying acoustic phonons, significantly reducing the lattice thermal conduction along the stacking direction.  As a consequence of this bonding hierarchy (i.e., coexisting rigid and fluctuating sublattices), BaAu2P4 exhibits a large power factor and low lattice thermal cond., which results in a high thermoelec. figure of merit (zT).  Thus, the authors' findings should encourage the exploration of new thermoelec. materials in the family of layered compds. with small band gaps and crystallog. heterogeneity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104822"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper thiocyanate (CuSCN) has recently received considerable attention because of its high hole mobility and applications in solar cells [Science 358(2017)768].         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Thermoelec. materials have attracted significant research interest in recent decades due to their promising application potential in interconverting heat and electricity.  Unfortunately, the strong coupling between the material parameters that det. thermoelec. efficiency, i.e., the Seebeck coeff., elec. cond., and thermal cond., complicates the optimization of thermoelec. energy converters.  Main-group chalcogenides provide a rich playground to alleviate the interdependence of these parameters.  Interestingly, only a subgroup of octahedrally coordinated chalcogenides possesses good thermoelec. properties.  This subgroup is also characterized by other outstanding characteristics suggestive of an exceptional bonding mechanism, which has been coined metavalent bonding.  This conclusion is further supported by a map that separates different bonding mechanisms.  In this map, all octahedrally coordinated chalcogenides with good performance as thermoelecs. are located in a well-defined region, implying that the map can be utilized to identify novel thermoelecs.  To unravel the correlation between chem. bonding mechanism and good thermoelec. properties, the consequences of this unusual bonding mechanism on the band structure are analyzed.  It is shown that features such as band degeneracy and band anisotropy are typical for this bonding mechanism, as is the low lattice thermal cond.         </div><div class="casAbstract">For decades, the three-phonon scattering process has been considered to govern thermal transport in solids, while the role of higher-order four-phonon scattering has been persistently unclear and so ignored.However, recent quant. calcns. of three-phonon scattering have often shown a significant overestimation of thermal cond. as compared to exptl. values.  In this Rapid Communication we show that four-phonon scattering is generally important in solids and can remedy such discrepancies.  For silicon and diamond, the predicted thermal cond. is reduced by 30% at 1000 K after including four-phonon scattering, bringing predictions in excellent agreement with measurements.  For the projected ultrahigh-thermal cond. material, zinc-blende BAs, a competitor of diamond as a heat sink material, four-phonon scattering is found to be strikingly strong as three-phonon processes have an extremely limited phase space for scattering.  The four-phonon scattering reduces the predicted thermal cond. from 2200 to 1400 W/m K at room temp.  The redn. at 1000 K is 60%.  We also find that optical phonon scattering rates are largely affected, being important in applications such as phonon bottlenecks in equilibrating electronic excitations.  Recognizing that four-phonon scattering is expensive to calc., in the end we provide some guidelines on how to quickly assess the significance of four-phonon scattering, based on energy surface anharmonicity and the scattering phase space.  Our work clears the decades-long fundamental question of the significance of higher-order scattering, and points out ways to improve thermoelecs., thermal barrier coatings, nuclear materials, and radiative heat transfer.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.100.245203"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruan, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stronger role of four-phonon scattering than three-phonon scattering in thermal conductivity of III-V semiconductors at room temperature</span>. <i>Phys. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dronskowski, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">LOBSTER: A tool to extract chemical bonding from plane-wave based DFT</span>. <i>J. Comput. Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>37</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">11</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1030</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1035</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/jcc.24300</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">LOBSTER: A tool to extract chemical bonding from plane-wave based DFT</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Maintz, Stefan; Deringer, Volker L.; Tchougreeff, Andrei L.; Dronskowski, Richard</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Computational Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">37</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1030-1035</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCCHDD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0192-8651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The computer program LOBSTER (Local Orbital Basis Suite Towards Electronic-Structure Reconstruction) enables chem.-bonding anal. based on periodic plane-wave (PAW) d.-functional theory (DFT) output and is applicable to a wide range of first-principles simulations in solid-state and materials chem.  LOBSTER incorporates analytic projection routines described previously in this very journal [J. Comput. Chem. 2013, 34, 2557] and offers improved functionality.  It calcs., among others, atom-projected densities of states (pDOS), projected crystal orbital Hamilton population (pCOHP) curves, and the recently introduced bond-weighted distribution function (BWDF).  The software is offered free-of-charge for non-com. research. © 2016 The Authors.  Journal of Computational Chem. Published by Wiley Periodicals, Inc.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref53" class="rightTabRefNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit53" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijheatmasstransfer.2022.122908"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruan, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Abnormal in-plane thermal conductivity anisotropy in bilayer α-phase tellurene</span>. <i>Int. J. Heat Mass Transfer</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>192</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">122908</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.ijheatmasstransfer.2022.122908</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Abnormal in-plane thermal conductivity anisotropy in bilayer α-phase tellurene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Yanhua; Yang, Xiaolong; Han, Zherui; Wu, Wenzhuo; Luo, Xiaobing; Ruan, Xiulin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Heat and Mass Transfer</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">192</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">122908</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IJHMAK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0017-9310</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In layered materials, it is well known that the cross-plane or cross-chain (CC) thermal cond. is lower than that of the in-plane or along-chain direction due to weaker bonding in the cross-plane or CC directions.  In this work, surprisingly, we predict using first-principles that the CC thermal cond. κ.perp. is higher than the along-chain thermal cond. κ‖ with a κ.perp./κ‖ ratio of 1.174 in bilayer α-phase tellurene (2L-αTe), an emerging 2D material that has recently drawn extensive interest due to its intriguing electronic, thermoelectronic, and piezoelectronic properties.  Also, the room-temp. κ.perp. and κ‖ of 2L-αTe are 5.69 W/mK and 4.85 W/mK, which are 251% and 31% enhanced from that of bulk Te, resp.  A detailed anal. of lattice structure, phonon spectra, and electron properties of 2L-αTe and bulk Te is provided.  We find that the larger lattice shrink in CC direction and the change in band angle lead to stiffened phonons and weaker anharmonicity, which in turn yield higher phonon group velocity and longer phonon lifetime in CC direction for 2L-αTe, resulting in the enhanced thermal cond. and the anomolus thermal anisotropy.  Crystal orbital Hamiltan population (COHP) and electron localization function (ELF) anal. demonstrate the enhancement of the strength of "covalent-like quasi-bonding" (CLQB) in CC direction of 2L-αTe, which is accompanied by the lattice shrink in CC direction and the change of band angle.  Our study identifies a case of unexpected anisotropic thermal transport in 2D materials, and sheds light on the improvement of thermal cond. isotropy in 2D materials for the thermal management of electronic devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref54" class="rightTabRefNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit54" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms4525"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Esfarjani, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Resonant bonding leads to low lattice thermal conductivity</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3525</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms4525</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Resonant bonding leads to low lattice thermal conductivity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee Sangyeop; Zhou Jiawei; Tian Zhiting; Chen Gang; Esfarjani Keivan; Luo Tengfei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3525</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Understanding the lattice dynamics and low thermal conductivities of IV-VI, V2-VI3 and V materials is critical to the development of better thermoelectric and phase-change materials.  Here we provide a link between chemical bonding and low thermal conductivity.  Our first-principles calculations reveal that long-ranged interaction along the 〈100〉 direction of the rocksalt structure exist in lead chalcogenides, SnTe, Bi2Te3, Bi and Sb due to the resonant bonding that is common to all of them.  This long-ranged interaction in lead chalcogenides and SnTe cause optical phonon softening, strong anharmonic scattering and large phase space for three-phonon scattering processes, which explain why rocksalt IV-VI compounds have much lower thermal conductivities than zincblende III-V compounds.  The new insights on the relationship between resonant bonding and low thermal conductivity will help in the development of better thermoelectric and phase change materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.0c01710"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sato, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tobita, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kimura, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mori, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unusual Lattice Dynamics and Anisotropic Thermal Conductivity in In<sub>2</sub>Te<sub>5</sub> Due to a Layered Structure and Planar-Coordinated Te-Chains</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">5335</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5342</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemmater.0c01710</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unusual Lattice Dynamics and Anisotropic Thermal Conductivity in In2Te5 Due to a Layered Structure and Planar-Coordinated Te-Chains</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenhao; Sato, Naoki; Tobita, Kazuki; Kimura, Kaoru; Mori, Takao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5335-5342</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Searching for novel materials with intrinsically low thermal cond. and uncovering their origin is an essential way to realize high performance in various energy-related applications, including thermoelecs.  Understanding the role of different structural features in materials can assist us in designing thermal transport properties.  Herein, we report thermal transport behavior of In2Te5, which is closely related to its layered zigzag structure and bonding in planar-coordinated Te-chains.  The exptl. thermal cond. shows significant anisotropy for the measured two directions and an extremely low value in the interlayer direction of about 0.3 W m-1 K-1 at 673 K.  The theor. calcns. of lattice thermal cond. based on d. functional theory support this behavior, and furthermore, they even reveal unprecedented anisotropy in the in-layer direction.  We demonstrate that these thermal transport behaviors can be attributed to resonant bonding and lattice dynamics obsd. at the Te atoms in the planar-coordinated environment.  Particularly strikingly, we discover a counterintuitive large pos. and neg. split of the Born effective charge (+8.7 and -5.1) at the adjacent Te atoms bonded covalently within the same plane.  They induce a significant dipole interaction in the x-direction.  Optical phonons are significantly softened in the specific direction by these characteristics in the Te-plane, which leads to large anisotropy in thermal transport.  Our findings should encourage further excavation of novel features in lattice dynamics out of unexplored materials with complex structures.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref56" class="rightTabRefNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit56" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.101.035901"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morelli, D. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jovovic, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Heremans, J. P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Intrinsically Minimal Thermal Conductivity in Cubic I-V- VI2 Semiconductors</span>. <i>Phys. Rev. Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2008</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>101</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">035901</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1103/PhysRevLett.101.035901</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intrinsically minimal thermal conductivity in cubic I-V-VI2 semiconductors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Morelli, D. T.; Jovovic, V.; Heremans, J. P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">101</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">035901/1-035901/4</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0031-9007</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report measurements of the thermal cond. of high-quality crystals of the cubic I-V-VI2 semiconductors AgSbTe2 and AgBiSe2.  The thermal cond. is temp. independent from 80 to 300 K at a value of approx. 0.70 W/mK.  Heat conduction is dominated by the lattice term, which we show is limited by umklapp and normal phonon-phonon scattering processes to a value that corresponds to the min. possible, where the phonon mean free path equals the interat. distance.  Min. thermal cond. in cubic I-V-VI2 semiconductors is due to an extreme anharmonicity of the lattice vibrational spectrum that gives rise to a high Gruneisen parameter and strong phonon-phonon interactions.  Members of this family of compds. are therefore most promising for thermoelec. applications, particularly as p-type materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i2">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acs.jpclett.2c03061?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acs.jpclett.2c03061</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">The method of unified theory (Theoretical formulation), lattice constants (Table S1), heat capacities (Figure S1), MFP of <i>b</i> and <i>c</i> axes (Figure S2), and cumulative directional <i>κ</i><sub><i>ph</i></sub> as a function of phonon MFP (Figure S3) for NaVO<sub>3</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.jpclett.2c03061/suppl_file/jz2c03061_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.jpclett.2c03061/suppl_file/jz2c03061_si_001.pdf">jz2c03061_si_001.pdf (555.14 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="93187dcd8d35075b-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>
